- 2026-06-01T16:58:32Z · Mac (device 1) · fix Mac/Safari-only worklist glitch — only the BOTTOM engagement row highlights on hover (and every row-click navigates to it). Root cause: the full-row stretched-link `after:absolute after:inset-0` overlay is anchored to `<TableRow className="relative">`, but WebKit does NOT treat `position:relative` on a `<tr>` as a containing block (Chrome/FF do), so every row's overlay escapes to the nearest honored ancestor — the `relative` table-container `<div>` (ui/table.tsx:11) — and they stack; the last row's overlay sits on top of the whole table. Fix: drop the full-row overlay; the engagement title becomes a normal link (hover + focus-visible underline). · locked: `src/components/dashboard/engagements-worklist.tsx` · branch: claude/worklist-row-highlight-safari · done · 2026-06-01T17:04:23Z — PR #366 merged (squash). className/comment-only change: removed the full-row stretched-link overlay; engagement title is now a plain link w/ hover + focus-visible underline; dropped vestigial `relative z-10` on the actions button. worklist tests 7/7 + tsc + eslint clean. Vercel auto-deploys main. NOTE: whole-row left-click intentionally dropped (never worked on Safari); title link + right-click menu + … menu remain. Mechanism: WebKit doesn't make `position:relative` `<tr>` a containing block, so the per-row overlays escaped + stacked.

ROOT CAUSES: (Bug 2 viewer) PortalImageLightbox renders INLINE inside ItemCard and is NOT createPortal'd to body; each ItemCard carries a persistent transform (`.animate-in-stagger > *` = `fade-up ... both`, whose end-state `translateY(0)` is a non-none transform) which establishes a CONTAINING BLOCK, so the lightbox's `fixed inset-0` resolves to the (tall, many-file) card box, not the viewport -> opens trapped in-row + `body{overflow:hidden}` scroll-lock = "frozen". - 2026-06-12T17:25:52Z · Mac (device 1) · BUG (founder): "Download all (ZIP)" on an engagement fails with toast "Couldnt prepare the download" (download_all_failed). DIAGNOSED by inspection (could NOT repro against prod — service-role PII read correctly blocked): src/app/api/engagements/[id]/files.zip/route.ts logs bulk_download BEFORE building, and the activity feed shows it logged → failure is in the BUILD (a 500). Route fetches EVERY uploaded_files row (NO is_duplicate / status filter) SEQUENTIALLY then zipSync level-6 deflates ALL bytes in memory under maxDuration=60. On a heavily-tested engagement (many repeated uploads incl. byte-identical duplicates + large phone photos) that blows the time/memory budget. FIX (no behavior loss): (a) skip is_duplicate files (byte-identical re-uploads = noise; original kept); (b) fetch bytes in BOUNDED PARALLEL (concurrency 6) instead of serial; (c) zipSync level 0 (STORE) — payload is already-compressed PDF/JPEG so deflate just burns CPU/time; (d) null-safe entry name (macZipEntryName(undefined) would throw); (e) wrap build in try/catch → clean 500 JSON + console.error (was an opaque crash). zip.ts buildZipArchive gains a level param (default 0) — also used by firm export.zip (same pre-compressed payload, fine). - 2026-06-12T17:41:47Z · Mac (device 1) · BUG STILL OPEN (founder retried post-#547, same "couldnt prepare the download" error). REAL ROOT CAUSE FOUND (my #547 fix was wrong): the hosting platform caps a BUFFERED serverless-function RESPONSE at ~4.5MB (documented all over the upload routes — the chunked-upload flow exists to dodge this exact cap). files.zip returned ONE buffered Uint8Array (new Response(zipBytes) + fixed Content-Length), so any engagement whose docs total >4.5MB fails. Single-file download works because /api/files/[id] STREAMS (new Response(upstream.body)). My #547 store(level 0) made the body BIGGER → could only worsen a cap failure. FIX: stream the zip via a chunked ReadableStream (new zipToStream() in zip.ts) exactly like single-file download — a streamed response is NOT subject to the buffered cap. Zip still built whole in memory (macOS-safe zipSync); just delivered in 256KB chunks. Keeps #547 skip-dup + parallel-fetch. NOTE: the 4.5MB cap is PLATFORM-only (does NOT exist on local next dev) so it cannot be reproduced locally — verified the streaming MECHANISM via a >4.5MB round-trip unit test (bytes identical, multi-chunk); founder confirms on prod. Could NOT read prod (PII guardrail blocked service-role reads twice — correct). · locked: src/app/api/engagements/[id]/files.zip/route.ts, src/lib/zip.ts(+test) · branch: claude/stream-zip-download · done · 2026-06-12T17:47Z — PR #549 MERGED (squash c3d03a5), Vercel preview SUCCESS, prod deploying. - 2026-07-14T22:20Z · PC (device 2) · BUGFIX (founder: 'Waiting on clients' stat shows 0 despite many engagements waiting on files). ROOT CAUSE verified live in founder's Chrome: isWaitingOnClient required itemsReadyToReview===0 AND flaggedFilesCount===0 — but an AUTO-REJECTED file (ball already back w/ client, client notified) counts as an ai-bounce in itemsReadyToReview AND in flaggedFiles, so e.g. Personal Tax (T4 auto-rejected + 4 pending items, NOTHING on accountant's plate) read as not-waiting. - 2026-07-17T03:20Z · PC (device 2) · PORTAL CRAWLER/LEAK ARMOUR SHIPPED (#784, e4dcdbf). Founder: "add security measures to prevent crawlers... the client portal is our main thing". INVESTIGATED FIRST — most of the defence already exists and is GOOD: tokens are nanoid(43) over 62-char alphabet = ~256 bits (guessing is a non-threat, so NO page-level rate limiter added — it would only risk throttling legit clients on shared NATs); ALL 16 portal API routes already rate-limited per-token AND per-IP (PORTAL_* specs in rate-limit.ts, fail-open without Upstash); oracle-proof 404s; MIME-allowlisted uploads; SITE-WIDE securityHeaders in next.config.ts (XFO DENY / nosniff / HSTS / Referrer-Policy strict-origin-when-cross-origin) that I did not know existed until reading the config. THE REAL GAPS were header-layer: (1) X-Robots-Tag on /r/*, /api/portal/*, /invite/* both locale spellings — the earlier noindex (#782) is a META TAG in page HTML; a PDF/JPEG response CANNOT carry a meta tag, so the actual tax documents (files/thumb/invoices/deliverables routes) had NO robots directive at all; (2) Referrer-Policy: no-referrer on token routes (the URL IS the credential; site-wide policy already keeps tokens out of cross-origin referers, this kills the same-origin trail too); (3) Cross-Origin-Resource-Policy: same-origin on /api/portal/* so a leaked file URL can't be hotlinked cross-origin (browser refuses; all legit consumers — portal page, pdf.js range requests, thumbs — are same-origin). KEY ORDERING FACT: Next applies matching header rules in array order, LAST WRITE PER KEY, so the token rules sit AFTER the /:path* catch-all and their Referrer-Policy wins. CHECKED BEFORE CHOOSING XFO: nothing iframes the portal or portal files (firm-side viewer is react-pdf/canvas via fetch, not iframe; SignWell iframes THEIR page into ours, their headers govern) so existing DENY stays. next.config.ts is ASK-FIRST shared config — touched on founder's explicit request, additive-only. VERIFIED live in prod on all 5 route shapes; /help keeps strict-origin-when-cross-origin and NO X-Robots-Tag (stays indexable). Battery: tsc 0, 1911 tests (main had grown — Mac shipped more), build green. NOT DONE (flagged, not built): CSP with nonces (high-risk to retrofit on Next inline scripts, separate task if wanted); portal page-level rate limit (see entropy note above). · status: done · 2026-07-17T03:20Z
